=100  \\$aRobinson, James$4edt$927642
=245  \\$aThe British Museum Citole. New Perspectives
=260  \\$c2015$aLondon$bThe British Museum
=300  \\$a156 pages
=500  \\$aThe British Museum citole is a unique example of medieval craftsmanship and is one of very few instruments from the Middle Ages to have survived. Its long, complex history includes a connection with the court of Elizabeth I and its conversion to a violin. The essays in this volume are the results of a conference held to highlight recent research, conservation work and scientific findings specifically related to the British Museum citole. The book enhances our understanding of one of the British Museum’s most celebrated objects by drawing together experts from the fields of history, art history, music, organology, conservation and science and performance practice. The result is a more developed understanding of the object within a wider historical context.

=245  \\$a法隆寺 (Hōryū-ji Temple)
=300  \\$a78 pages
=500  \\$aHōryū-ji (Japanese: 法隆寺; lit. 'Temple of the Flourishing Dharma') is a Buddhist temple that was once one of the powerful Seven Great Temples, located in Ikaruga, Nara Prefecture, Japan. Built shortly after Buddhism was introduced to Japan, it is also one of the oldest Buddhist sites in the country. Its full name is Hōryū Gakumonji (法隆学問寺), or Learning Temple of the Flourishing Law, with the complex serving as both a seminary and monastery.

=100  \\$4cmp$aBeethoven, Ludwig van$d1770-1827$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q255$95335
=245  \\$aBeethoven's "Eroica" Sketchbook
=260  \\$aIllinois$bUniversity of Illinois Press$c2013
=300  \\$a2 vols.
=520  \\$aAmong Beethoven's many surviving sketchbooks, one of the most famous is the "Eroica" Sketchbook, containing all the known sketches for the "Eroica" Symphony, the "Waldstein" Sonata, and other works of 180304. These include his first sketches for the opera Leonore (later entitled Fidelio), as well as the unfinished opera Vestas Feuer, the oratorio Christus am Oelberge, the Triple Concerto, songs, keyboard compositions, and early sketches that later bore fruit in the Fourth Piano Concerto and the Fifth and Sixth Symphonies. It also contains ideas for works that were never completed. This edition makes available both a complete facsimile and transcription of the sketchbook for the first time, along with a detailed commentary on the origins, contents, and significance of this vitally important source.

=041  \\$afre$ager
=059  \\$apf
=100  \\$aFahrbach Junior, Philipp $d1845-1894$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2086690$4cmp$920199
=245  \\$aLes soirées de Pesth.$bcélèbre répertoire du cappelmeister Fahrbach. Valses, Polkas, Galops, Mazurkas, Marches.
=246  \1$bTrente Danses Choisies du célèbre Cappelmeister Philippe Fahrbach junior
=260  \\$aParis$bAu Ménestrel$cs.d.
=300  \\$a[vi]-187 pages$bleather bound, gilded embossed spine, marbled endpapers, lithography
=500  \\$aPhilipp Fahrbach the Younger was an Vienese violinist and conductor, son of Fahrbach the Elder. He succeeded his father as conductor of his orchestra in 1855, with whom he celebrated great triumphs at the Paris World Exhibition in 1878. He was regarded as a rival to Johann Strauss (son) and composed over 500 dances, marches and operettas. 
=500  \\$aHe was introduced to the public at the age of 11, and took up the position of bandmaster in Budapest and also in Vienna. He undertook concert tours to Berlin, Paris and Madrid and many of his works were first published by French publishers (hence the titles). Like his father most of his works are to be found in archives for piano, the amount of orchestral material available being s rather limited; much of what is left has been played, or arranged for small ensembles from the piano edition.
=500  \\$acollection of dances  in piano score, all titels in German original as well as translated in French

=500  \\$aAndré Jaspar was a Belgian composer and conductor. He studied cello with the priest Ferdinand Harzeus, and later performed as a cellist in the semi-amateur string quartets of Liège. In 1821-1826 he was in charge of the music school, which was dissolved due to the opening of the Liège Conservatoire in 1827; Jaspar refused the position of professor of solfeggio offered to him at the Conservatoire. From 1830 he performed in Liège as an orchestral and choral conductor.

=100  \\$aSaint-Sevin dit L'Abbé le Fils, Joseph-Barnabé$d1727-1803$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1706326$921040
=245  10$aPrincipes du violon
=260  \\$aGeneva$bMinkoff$c2001
=300  \\$a81 pages of music$c30 cm
=500  \\$a"Réimpression de l'édition de Paris, 1776"--T.p. verso. This ed. with the original imprint L'Auteur and Le Clerc marchand rue Saint Honoré is dated 1761 in reference sources. The Minkoff reprint date 1976 on the title page could indicate that the present ed. is be a reissue of an earlier Minkoff ed. with that reprint date, however that ed. appears in bibliographic records as a reprint of the 1772 ed.
=590  \\$apour apprendre le doigté de cet instrument, et les différens agrémens dont il est susceptible. Dédiés à Monsieur le Marquis de Rodoüan de Damartin, Mousquetaire de la Seconde Compagnie de la Garde du Roi. Par Mr. l'Abbé le Fils, Ordinaire de l'Académie Royale de Musique. Ces principes sont suivis de deux suites d'airs d'opéra à deux violons, dont le choix lui a paru le meilleur, de plusieurs leçons dans le genre de sonates avec la basse chiffrée pour le clavessin, d'exemples analogues à ces leçons, de préludes dans les tons majeurs et mineurs, et d'une suite de jolis airs variés pour un Violon seul. Les Personnes qui joüent du Par-dessus-de-Viole à quatre cordes peuvent faire usage de ces Principes, en observant seulement de donner aux Lettres t et p une signification contraire à celle que l'on trouvera dans ce Livre.

=520  \\$aHet Apollohuis (English: The Apollo House) was a space for experimental music and visual arts, "focused in particular on...sound art, new music, performance art and the new media," founded in Eindhoven, Netherlands, by Remko Scha and Paul Panhuysen in a former 19th century cigar factory in 1980. Partly funded by their own publishing house, the space was closed in 2001 after their grant was discontinued.

"Between 1980 and 2001, Het Apollohuis organized 253 art exhibitions, 476 concerts and performances, 46 public lectures, symposia and several festivals (as "ECHO: images of sound II" in 1987 [2] or FLEA Festival in 1997). Artists-in-residence, asked to create an exhibition, an installation or a publication, where provided with an apartment, studio space, and materials. Known artists that had events at the Apollohuis were for instance Ellen Fullman, Glenn Branca, Michel Waisvisz, Pauline Oliveros, Pierre Bastien, The Hub (band), Nicolas Collins, Maciunas Ensemble.
